## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard dependent variable in chemical kinetics ODEs. With only A and t available, the most likely relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where reaction rate depends on concentration (reaction order), possibly with time-varying effective rate constants or approach-to-equilibrium behavior.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-saturated or constant-flux input/removal)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, many elementary steps under pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products, or effective second-order in A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (generalized empirical reaction order; fits complex mechanisms)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating kinetics with limiting capacity or depletion of another species folded into c1)
- Approach to equilibrium (relaxation): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (first-order relaxation toward steady state A = c1; can represent reversible net rate in a reduced model)
- Mixed-order (linear + quadratic): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel pathways or termination + propagation contributions)
- Inhibited / saturating consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases with A but saturates; effective limitation such as site saturation or transport-limited step)
- Autocatalysis with baseline loss: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) - c2 * A (autocatalytic production plus first-order decay/removal)
- Time-varying first-order (exponential drift in k): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant changes over time; e.g., ramping conditions or catalyst activation/deactivation captured phenomenologically)
- Time-varying source + decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A (time-dependent feed/photogeneration plus first-order consumption)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., chopped illumination): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (rate modulated periodically in time; still proportional to A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reactant consumption typically enforces dA_dt ≤ 0 for A ≥ 0; models often include a leading negative sign times a nonnegative function of A.
- First-order kinetics correspond to dA_dt proportional to A, implying a constant fractional decay rate (straight line in log(A) vs t when integrated).
- Higher reaction order shows increasing sensitivity at high A (e.g., A**2 makes early-time decay much faster when A is large).
- Terms like (c1 - A) indicate relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1, with the sign switching depending on whether A is below or above c1.
- Autocatalytic forms A*(c1 - A) encode self-acceleration at low A and self-limitation at high A, producing sigmoidal time courses after integration.
- Rational forms A/(A + c1) represent saturation of rate at high A, consistent with finite site/active-area limits or transport bottlenecks.
- Explicit time dependence in the prefactor (e.g., exp(c*t), sin(c*t)) indicates changing external conditions (temperature ramps, light intensity modulation, catalyst deactivation/activation) that alter an effective rate constant.
- Additive combinations of different powers of A (e.g., A and A**2) often indicate parallel pathways or multiple controlling steps contributing to the net rate.
- Including a constant source term (e.g., +c0 or +c0*exp(c1*t)) models feed, generation, or baseline production that can balance consumption and create nonzero steady states.

So any matching candidate must (i) be independent of \(t\), (ii) contain a \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) term with the correct amplitude, and (iii) have exactly the quadratic and linear polynomial parts with those coefficients, with **no extra non-polynomial dependence on A** (like \(A/(A c+1)\), \(1/(A c+d)\), \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), \(\exp(\cdot)\), \(\log(\exp(\cdot)+1)\), \(|A|\), Max, etc.), unless those can be made identically constant/zero for all A by parameter choice.

A key obstruction: many candidates use **sin(log(...)+phase)**, but GT needs **cos(log(A+1))**. While \(\cos(x)=\sin(x+\pi/2)\), the candidates’ inner log is typically \(\log(c\cdot|A|+1)\), not \(\log(A+1)\). Because of the **Abs(A)**, you cannot make \(\log(c|A|+1)\equiv \log(A+1)\) for all real A. Even if you restrict to \(A\ge 0\), the task requires equality for all values of the feature variables, so Abs breaks equivalence.

Also, any rational term like \(A/(A c+1)\) or \(1/(A c+d)\) cannot be made into a polynomial (or a constant) for all A unless you choose parameters that make it undefined or still A-dependent; the only way to remove it is to set its coefficient to 0—but in these candidates it appears with fixed coefficient 1, so it cannot be removed.
